= 100 * time.Millisecond\n65: \n66: \t// podAttachAndMountTimeout is the maximum amount of time the\n67: \t// WaitForAttachAndMount call will wait for all volumes in the specified pod\n68: \t// to be attached and mounted. Even though cloud operations can take several\n69: \t// minutes to complete, we set the timeout to 2 minutes because kubelet\n70: \t// will retry in the next sync iteration. This frees the associated\n71: \t// goroutine of the pod to process newer updates if needed (e.g., a delete\n72: \t// request to the pod).\n73: \t// Value is slightly offset from 2 minutes to make timeouts due to this\n74: \t// constant recognizable.\n75: \tpodAttachAndMountTimeout = 2*time.Minute + 3*time.Second\n76: \n77: \t// podAttachAndMountRetryInterval is the amount of time the GetVolumesForPod\n78: \t// call waits before retrying\n79: \tpodAttachAndMountRetryInterval = 300 * time.Millisecond\n80: \n81: \t// waitForAttachTimeout is the maximum amount of time a\n82: \t// operationexecutor.Mount call will wait for a volume to be attached.\n83: \t// Set to 10 minutes because we've seen attach operations take several\n84: \t// minutes to complete for some volume plugins in some cases. While this\n85: \t// operation is waiting it only blocks other operations on the same device,\n86: \t// other devices are not affected.\n87: \twaitForAttachTimeout = 10 * time.Minute\n88: )\n89: \n90: // VolumeManager runs a set of asynchronous loops that figure out which volumes\n91: // need to be attached/mounted/unmounted/detached based on the pods scheduled on\n92: // this node and makes it so.\n93: type VolumeManager interface {\n94: \t// Starts the volume manager and all the asynchronous loops that it controls\n95: \tRun(ctx context.Context, sourcesReady config.SourcesReady)\n96: \n97: \t// WaitForAttachAndMount processes the volumes referenced in the specified\n98: \t// pod and blocks until they are all attached and mounted (reflected in\n99: \t// actual state of the world).\n100: \t// An error is returned if all volumes are not attached and mounted within\n101: \t// the duration defined in podAttachAndMountTimeout.\n102: \tWaitForAttachAndMount(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) error\n103: \n104: \t// WaitForUnmount processes the volumes referenced in the specified\n105: \t// pod and blocks until they are all unmounted (reflected in the actual\n106: \t// state of the world).\n107: \t// An error is returned if all volumes are not unmounted within\n108: \t// the duration defined in podAttachAndMountTimeout.\n109: \tWaitForUnmount(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) error\n110: \n111: \t// WaitForAllPodsUnmount is a version of WaitForUnmount that blocks and\n112: \t// waits until all the volumes belonging to all the pods are unmounted.\n113: \t// An error is returned if there's at least one Pod with volumes not unmounted\n114: \t// within the duration defined in podAttachAndMountTimeout.\n115: \tWaitForAllPodsUnmount(ctx context.Context, pods []*v1.Pod) error\n116: \n117: \t// GetMountedVolumesForPod returns a VolumeMap containing the volumes\n118: \t// referenced by the specified pod that are successfully attached and\n119: \t// mounted. The key in the map is the OuterVolumeSpecName (i.e.\n120: \t// pod.Spec.Volumes[x].Name). It returns an empty VolumeMap if pod has no\n121: \t// volumes.\n122: \tGetMountedVolumesForPod(podName types.UniquePodName) container.VolumeMap\n123: \n124: \t// GetPossiblyMountedVolumesForPod returns a VolumeMap containing the volumes\n125: \t// referenced by the specified pod that are either successfully attached\n126: \t// and mounted or are \"uncertain\", i.e. a volume plugin may be mounting\n127: \t// them right now. The key in the map is the OuterVolumeSpecName (i.e.\n128: \t// pod.Spec.Volumes[x].Name). It returns an empty VolumeMap if pod has no\n129: \t// volumes.\n130: \tGetPossiblyMountedVolumesForPod(podName types.UniquePodName) container.VolumeMap\n131: \n132: \t// GetExtraSupplementalGroupsForPod returns a list of the extra\n133: \t// supplemental groups for the Pod. These extra supplemental groups come\n134: \t// from annotations on persistent volumes that the pod depends on.\n135: \tGetExtraSupplementalGroupsForPod(pod *v1.Pod) []int64\n136: \n137: \t// GetVolumesInUse returns a list of all volumes that implement the volume.Attacher\n138: \t// interface and are currently in use according to the actual and desired\n139: \t// state of the world caches. A volume is considered \"in use\" as soon as it\n140: \t// is added to the desired state of world, indicating it *should* be\n141: \t// attached to this node and remains \"in use\" until it is removed from both\n142: \t// the desired state of the world and the actual state of the world, or it\n143: \t// has been unmounted (as indicated in actual state of world).\n144: \tGetVolumesInUse() []v1.UniqueVolumeName\n145: \n146: \t// ReconcilerStatesHasBeenSynced returns true only after the actual states in reconciler\n147: \t// has been synced at least once after kubelet starts so that it is safe to update mounted\n148: \t// volume list retrieved from actual state.\n149: \tReconcilerStatesHasBeenSynced() bool\n150: \n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0@d17b464c6fcd3273e4b1f695890bf0af7d5b272d/-/blob/pkg/kubelet/volumemanager/volume_manager.go%3FL1-150"}}}
